# Project Nyx — Backlog

A running list of items intentionally deferred from the current build sequence. This is the destination for anything that would otherwise be said as "let's log that for the future."

**Access:** PM can type `view backlog`, `show backlog`, or any natural-language equivalent in a session — Claude reads this file and presents it grouped by priority, surfacing anything that blocks the current build phase first.

**Adding items:** Claude adds rows here proactively — do not wait for PM. When raising a "for the future" item mid-session, write it here before continuing. Include a one-line _why_ so future-you can re-evaluate without re-deriving the context.

**IDs:** sequential `B-NNN`. Never reuse. When closing an item, leave the row and mark `Status: Done — <session date>` rather than deleting.

**Priority:**
- **Now** — should be tackled in the current or next session; here only because it's outside the in-flight chunk
- **Next** — tackle within the next 2–3 sessions or the next build phase
- **Later** — real but not time-sensitive; revisit when conditions change (e.g. pre-prod, multi-pet, paid tier)

**Status — lead with a structured head.** The Status cell must **begin** with one state token from this fixed set, then the date and resolving PR, so the column reads true at a glance and drift is machine-checkable:

- `Open` — not started.
- `In progress — <date> (PR #N)` — actively being built; say what's left.
- `Partial — <date> (PR #N)` — a defined slice shipped, more deferred; name the remaining slices.
- `Blocked — <reason>` — can't proceed; state the blocker (usually an Open Question).
- `Done — <date> (PR #N)` — shipped. Keep the row (don't delete); never close without a resolving PR/session reference.

**Rewrite the head when state changes — do NOT append the update to the tail of an already-long cell.** The recurring drift this file suffers is exactly that: a row that *opens* with `draft PR #106` / `R1 slice scoped` while a `Done` marker sits buried 200 words later — so the column lies even though the truth is technically "in the row" (caught reactively as B-022/B-045 on 2026-05-31, B-040/B-051/B-075 on 2026-06-11). Narrative and history may stay **below** the head, but the first token must be current. `/wrap` Step 4 reconciles these rows for every B-ID a session touches; the `backlog-groomer` skill enforces the head.

---

| B-325 | Retroactive + med-first combo linking (the paths B-156 B2b left uncovered) | PM-flagged UX gap (2026-07-12): the med↔food combo link (`paired_event_id`) can ONLY be created on the FORWARD, in-the-moment path — the "+ Add a med given with this" line on the meal/treat completion card (`MealCompletionCard`), which auto-dismisses in ~5s. Code-confirmed: (a) an already-logged treat/meal has NO "add a med" affordance on its detail screen — the `ComboLinkRow` in `event/[id].tsx` + the History `ComboCrossLink` are READ-ONLY, rendering only a link that already exists; (b) the med side has NO combo entry at all — `MedicationCompletionCard` offers only adherence + the descriptive `how_given` (in_treat/in_food) chip, and `edit-event.tsx` has zero paired handling. So both owner-hypotheses hold: you can't add a med to an existing treat, and you can't attach a treat to an existing med. This reopens B-156's own false-adherence hole for the exact target user (Sam pilling a squirming cat misses the 5s window → the intake→adherence safety coupling from PR B3 never runs). Directions differ in weight: **med→EXISTING treat** is a clean reuse of `insertMedicationDose` + `pairedEventId` + the `getMealForEvent` vehicle-intake read (high value, cheap, safety-coupling reuses the forward path); **minting a NEW treat from the med side** forces the pure-vehicle-inflation question (investigation §8 / B-111) that the forward path sidesteps by construction (`how_given` already serves the label-only med-first case). Recommended shape: a retroactive "+ Add a med given with this" on the treat/meal DETAIL screen (a better home than the narrow card — §4) + a med-detail "link to an existing treat"; run the same B3 coupling on both; never mint a phantom vehicle event. | Next | 2026-07-12 | Rides the B-156 promotion decision; extends B-156 (combo); composes with B-176 (Today parity) / B-173 (ate-around-the-pill) | **Partial — direction ① shipped via #342 (2026-07-12); direction ② (med-first) still HELD (B-111).** PM-greenlit & designed via mockup rounds this session. The retroactive "+ Add a med given with this" entry now lives on the meal/treat detail screen (`app/event/[id].tsx`, gated on `food_type ∈ {meal,treat}`), routing to the same pre-bound picker (`comboSource:'detail'`) → linked dose via the existing `insertMedicationDose(…, pairedEventId)` + PR B3 coupling. Design (PM steer + Designer/persona call): no completion-card replay — returns to the treat; a **not-finished** vehicle gets a deliberate **confirm sheet** (`components/log/ComboDoseConfirmSheet.tsx`, heads-up + real adherence chips + "Not sure yet") so the owner inputs how much got in rather than landing silently unconfirmed; unconfirmed survives only as the explicit-skip fallback; adherence stays editable on the dose screen (G2). New `comboConfirmHeadsUp` copy helper (+tests). `adversarial-reviewer` PASS (never a false 'given' across backdrop/skip/write-fail/read-fail; forward path byte-for-byte unchanged); `code-reviewer` clean after token fix. | B-234 | Capture a real diet-start date, distinct from first-food-log | `feeding_arrangements.activeFrom` is set to when the owner first LOGGED the food, not when the diet actually started (B-233) — so the vet report can't legitimately show a mid-window diet START even when one really happened; it now conservatively renders every free-fed diet as "start not recorded." | B-235 | `buildConcurrentChanges` silently drops a confounder with a malformed non-null start date | `report.ts` `consider()` does `if (startDate !== null && startDn === null) return` — a medication/diet-trial with a corrupt (unparseable) start date vanishes from the GP-0 "Reading the trend" note entirely, the §4/B-117 silent-drop class (a confounder the diet then takes credit for). Unreachable for free-fed (always null now) and requires corrupt DB data for a med/trial, so low severity — but it's a silent-drop path with no test. Fix: render it as a standing "start not recorded" confounder (like free-fed) rather than dropping it, + a test. Surfaced by the B-233 adversarial pass. | Later | 2026-07-04 | — | Open. |

| B-245 | Large-Edge-Function deploy: strip/escape comments so a dashboard paste is byte-clean (B-225 addendum) | Deploying `generate-report` v7 (PR 7) via the dashboard paste left **cosmetic UTF-8 mojibake in source COMMENTS** (`§`→`Â§`, `—`→`â`) — harmless (comments don't execute; esbuild's `--charset=ascii` had already escaped all OUTPUT strings to `\uXXXX`, so the rendered report is byte-correct), but it makes a sha256 read-back diff noisy and would mask a real corruption. Fix on the `scripts/deploy-edge.sh` side: strip comments in the bundle step (esbuild `--legal-comments=none` + a comment-strip) or extend `--charset=ascii` to comments, so a dashboard paste round-trips byte-identically and the read-back sha matches. Composes with B-225 (durable large-function deploy path). Tooling/process, no clinical logic. | Later | 2026-07-05 | Any large-function dashboard redeploy | Open |
| B-246 | Vet report: chronicity flag episode-count/onset (56-day detector window) doesn't trace to the report-window Appendix A tally | The `symptom_chronicity` safety flag renders `episodeCount`/`firstOnsetIso` straight from the detector finding, which the engine computes over its OWN `chronicity.windowDays = 56` lookback — but the report window is up to 90 days and Appendix A tallies over the full window. When onset falls between the 56-day and window edges, the flag shows e.g. "14 episodes, first noted ~May 9" while the At-a-glance tile + Appendix A show "15 / May 6" — violating the report's own "every number traces to Appendix A" rule (§127) on the LEAD safety line. Same class as the round-1 chronicity 18-vs-19 local-day fix (which recounted `symptomDays` report-side but left `episodeCount`/`firstOnsetIso` on the detector's window) and the B-219 worsening-tz debt. Fix as ONE deliberate decision — report-side recount of the chronicity episode set within the report window vs. windowing the detector to the report — with a mandatory `adversarial-reviewer` pass (the counts sit at the ③/④ valve). Surfaced by the PR 7 `vet-report-cold-read`; NOT introduced by PR 7 (the chronicity flag render is untouched by that diff). | **Partial — the `daysSinceLastEpisode` slice CLOSED in PR 7 / #278 (2026-07-05):** the flag's "days since the most recent episode" now local-recounts over the same episode set as `symptomDays` (guarded by `episodeSetMatches`), so the lead safety flag no longer contradicts the At-a-glance tile (was "4 days ago" vs "5 d since" — the cold-read blocker); `adversarial-reviewer`-gated. **Still Open:** the `episodeCount`/`firstOnsetIso` 56d-detector-vs-report-window reconciliation. | Next | 2026-07-05 | Step 9/10 report↔detector window consistency | Partial |
| B-248 | Harden `nyx-vet-attachments` access — the same bucket-wide read hole as B-244 | `006_storage_policies.sql` grants ANY authenticated user `SELECT`/`INSERT`/`DELETE` on ANY object in `nyx-vet-attachments` (path-ownership app-layer only), the identical de-facto-shared-read pattern B-244 closed for `nyx-event-attachments`. | B-060 | `analyze-vomit` n=1 read reassures on the ABSENCE of a red flag | Shipped read text says "nothing obviously alarming is visible on its own" — reassuring on the *absence* of a red flag from a single sample, the exact sentence the n=1-never-reassures invariant forbids (B-013/B-027/`clinical-guardrails`). A first denylist attempt (`readTextReassures`) was **adversarial-FAILED** — a denylist must enumerate "the model asserted wellness", an open vocabulary (missed ~86% of plausible phrasings, nuked legit concern reads). Replaced with allowlist-by-construction: new pure `selectReadText` surfaces the model's free-text read ONLY on the `worth_a_call` escalation path (names a PRESENT flag — safe "escalate on presence"); the `monitor`/no-flag path returns a deterministic `buildMonitorReadText`, never the model's words → reassurance-on-absence closed BY CONSTRUCTION (adversarial sweep: monitor surfaces the model read 0/48 floor inputs). Prompt + read_text schema reworded off the absence framing. **adversarial-reviewer PASS** (rework); pure read-selection unit-tested. Residual: the model `description` field is still free-text on the monitor path → **B-179** (clinical-guardrails Ambiguity #2). Deno deploy gate (deno check/test + redeploy analyze-vomit, preserve verify_jwt) + stale-`read_text`-self-heals-on-reanalysis = PM action items. |

| B-081 | Detector ⑤ grazing-guard small-sample residual — tune on real data | The grazing guard is a relative check that collapses to the count floor at small N, so a grazer with ~3 witnessed vomits near a graze can fire on a ~7% coincidence (worst above-floor residual ~13–17%). Root cause is a §3.3 design tension, not a bug — the golden "4 of 12" is itself ~6%, so no fixed threshold fires it while suppressing a same-strength grazer. v1 mitigated (`minEligibleEpisodes=6`); once B-047 gives live FP data, decide whether to swap the `2× expected` proxy for a binomial-tail bar + recalibrate the golden. | Next | 2026-06-11 | B-078 merged; needs B-047 live FP data | Open || B-083 | Detector ⑥ time-of-day clustering — n=8 chance-cluster residual, tune on real data | The calibrated ⑥ floors (5 + 0.6) pass the §7 "≪5%" test pooled (~3.6%) but the n=8 slice alone fires at ~7.4% — because "5 of 8" (0.625) is exactly the golden the detector exists to fire. The residual is **intrinsic** (a chance and a real "5 of 8" are indistinguishable). Accepted for v1 (descriptive card, never reassures); the per-n=8 rate is made visible via a property-test assertion. Once B-047 gives live FP data, consider a circular scan-statistic + recalibrate the golden. | Next | 2026-06-11 | B-079 merged; needs B-047 live FP data | Open |

| B-138 | Medication-confounder (PR 9) calibration residuals — dose-point under-detection + incidental-drug over-suppression | Surfaced by the adversarial-reviewer on B-117 PR 9. Two ACCEPTED, safe-direction limitations of the §8 confounder pass — both logged for Data-Scientist/Dr. Chen calibration, neither a code bug, neither ever falsely reassures (the cardinal invariant held): **(a) dose-as-point under-detection** — an administered dose is modeled as a POINT in `[onset−W, onset]` (like a meal), so a once-daily LONG-ACTING, regimen-UNLINKED drug dosed > W hours before onset (e.g. 06:00 dose, 21:00 vomit, 12h vomit window) is invisible → the confounder isn't caught → a false food correlation can surface (UNDER-suppression). Safe direction (never reassurance; degrades to today's no-med behavior). Robust fix = the regimen SPAN, which only exists once a regimen is set up (doses are regimen-unlinked today, B-135); a dose-persistence/tail is the alternative but reintroduces an arbitrary window — a Dr. Chen window-shape call (composes with the B-135 revisit). **(b) incidental-drug over-suppression** — mirroring the free-fed standing cap, a single incidental/PRN dose in any matched window caps the finding at Early; reviewer Monte-Carlo (real beef→vomit pet + ~5 random PRN doses/40d) wrongly SUPPRESSES the real finding ~4.8% and caps it at Early ~55%. Conservative by design, but it bounds how often the pass nicks a real correlation for PRN/chronically-medicated pets (the diet-trial wedge). Decision for Data-Scientist/PM: tune (require a dose persistence/tail; or cap-not-suppress below a dose-count floor) or ratify as the conservative v1. NOTE: the higher-severity Bonferroni family-shrink tier-inflation the same review found was FIXED in PR 9 (`suppressedFamilyCount` keeps withdrawn candidates in the family + regression test), not deferred here. | Later | 2026-06-20 | Step 10 / B-117 PR 9 follow-up | Open — calibration, carries a Data-Scientist/PM call |

| B-178 | Edge Functions don't auto-deploy on merge → silent drift (post-merge deploy gate) | Surfaced 2026-06-24 by a PM-requested edge-function currency audit: `analyze-vomit`'s **B-028 (#220) merged 2026-06-22 but was never deployed** — the live function ran the month-old v4 (old inline write-back, missing the tested `buildAnalysisWriteBack` never-clobber guard) until this session caught + redeployed it (v5). Root cause: merging a PR that changes `supabase/functions/**` does NOT deploy it — deploys are a separate manual MCP step, so an Edge Function silently drifts from `main` until someone notices. Risk class: a merged clinical/extraction fix (e.g. an `analyze-vomit` escalation tweak, a `generate-signal` confounder fix) can sit un-live indefinitely. Options: (a) a CI job that deploys changed functions on merge to `main` (needs a `SUPABASE_ACCESS_TOKEN` cloud-env secret — weigh the standing credential vs the MCP path); (b) a lightweight **drift check** — periodically (or in `/wrap`) read back each live function's source sha and compare to a fresh bundle of on-disk source, flag mismatches; (c) a manual "did this PR touch an Edge Function? deploy it" checklist line in the merge ritual. | B-182 | Deterministic chronicity / persistence Signal lane — "ongoing for N weeks, unresolved" | The 2026-06-25 vet-council deep-dive (`docs/research/2026-06-vet-council-nyx-deep-dive.md`, Findings 2/3) found the single highest-value engine gap is also the most computable: the engine surfaces ④ worsening (a week-over-week bump) + ⑥ timing but is **silent on chronicity** — six weeks of unresolved ~q2-day vomiting reaches the owner as "3 this week, up from 2." All 5 specialist lenses independently named chronicity the *strongest* signal. Needs only an episode span + count under the existing honesty floors (the ④ shape), **no LLM**. Chronicity ≠ worsening (a flat-but-relentless course is invisible to ④). | B-188 | Harden detector ⑦ `activeWeeks` against the calendar-phase "barbell" (PR-2 work) | B-182 PR-1 adversarial review (2026-06-26) BROKE the distribution floor: `activeWeeks = floor((now − onset)/7d)` is **now-anchored**, so a 3-consecutive-day cluster lands in 1 OR 2 buckets by wall-clock phase. Two consequences — (a) a **two-cluster barbell** (3 stale + 3 recent, ~6 quiet weeks between) reaches `activeWeeks=3` via a bucket-edge straddle and fires, the exact two-endpoint/one-cluster shape §4.2/§4.3 claim it excludes; (b) identical data flips fire↔silent across calendar days (jarring on a safety surface). **Safe-direction (over-fire, never reassurance) and only the marginal activeWeeks=3 shape → NOT a merge-blocker; deferred from PR 1.** Fix in **B-182 PR 2** (adversarial-mandatory anyway) with a calendar-independent, straddle-robust distribution measure — note the simple re-anchors (`firstOnset` / fixed-UTC-week) kill the non-determinism but a consecutive-day cluster can still straddle a fixed 7-day edge, so the real fix counts distinct *bouts'* weeks phase-stably. Flag the §4.2 spec edit. | Next | 2026-06-26 | B-182 PR 2 (composition/ranking) | **Done — 2026-06-26 (PR #247)** — fixed in B-182 PR 2 with `countDistributionWeeks`: a phase-stable greedy ≥7-day-gap packing computed from onset data alone (never `now`). Closes both faults — a tight cluster counts as ONE distribution-week so a barbell → 2 (< minActiveWeeks 3, no straddle), and identical data is calendar-phase-invariant. Activity-selection-optimal so no false-negative under-count (adversarial-reviewer swept q5/q6-day courses + a 7-phase barbell regression held). §4.2 spec edit flagged as a Tier-2 doc follow-up (PM-gated, not yet written). |

| B-202 | Weight snapshot (`pets.weight_kg`) direct write has no offline retry | code-reviewer (2026-07-02, B-197): both the log path (`app/log.tsx`) and the new `updateWeightCheck` (`lib/weight.ts`) re-point the denormalized `pets.weight_kg` snapshot via a best-effort direct `supabase.from('pets').update(...)` with no queue/retry — an edit or log made offline silently fails to correct the snapshot, and nothing re-attempts until another weight write recomputes it. | B-207 | Full-screen photo viewer downloaded the multi-MB original (5–10s lag) | Tapping a vomit photo to view full-screen fetched the raw uncompressed original (4.48–6.47 MB) via a plain signed URL → 5–10s load (worse on first tap, before any cache). Raw-URL fallback on image error so a disabled transform add-on degrades to the old behaviour, never a blank photo. | Now | 2026-07-01 | — | Done — 2026-07-01 (PR #255) |

| B-212 | Generalize the medication workflow to "medications & supplements" | PM-floated during the vet-report spec (2026-07-02): OTC supplements (probiotics, joint/skin, etc.) are concurrent GI/health interventions a vet needs to see, but the B-117 medication model only carries prescribed drugs. | B-214 | Vet report: `hoursSinceLastFullMeal` uses UTC instants against a local-day window end | The B-213 "how long off food?" gap is `detNowMs − lastFullMs` (report.ts), UTC instants, while `detectionNowIso` for a **custom past window** is `<endDate>T23:59:59.999Z` (UTC end-of-day of a *local* end-date). In a western tz (e.g. UTC-10), a full meal logged local-evening of the window's end day has a UTC instant *after* that boundary → negative gap → `Math.max(0,…)` floors it to `0 h`. Bounded (≤ tz offset ~14 h), only bites meals genuinely near a custom-window end, and a multi-day gap can never be clamped short — but it under-states (the reassuring direction) for that sliver. Default cascade (window end = now) is unaffected. Fix = anchor the gap (and `detectionNowFor`) to the owner-local end-of-day. Surfaced by `adversarial-reviewer` on the B-213 PR (#263). | Later | 2026-07-03 | — | Open |
| B-215 | Vet report: intake meal-log assumes meal `occurredAt` is witnessed (no B-010 guard) | The B-213 recent-meals appendix (`intakeLogRow`) and the flag's "last full meal" line render meal times/dates as precise points, with no `occurredAtConfidence` guard — correct today only because rated meals are witnessed-by-invariant (the intake lane has no non-witnessed meal path). If a non-witnessed rated meal ever becomes possible, `fmtLocalTime` would print false precision. Latent, not live. Fix = carry meal confidence into the intake path and render a range/estimate like appendix A does for symptoms. Surfaced by `adversarial-reviewer` on the B-213 PR (#263). | Later | 2026-07-03 | — | Open |
| B-216 | Vet report: chronicity flag `activeWeeks` count doesn't reconcile with the span / trend chart | The B-182 chronicity safety flag reads "N episodes across **M weeks**" where M = `activeWeeks` (distinct now-anchored active-week buckets, B-188 phase-stable), but the same page shows a longer span (e.g. "ongoing 36 days") and a trend chart with more populated week-bars (6). Two non-reconciling week-counts on one page invite a vet to doubt the denominators. It **understates** chronicity (safe direction) and doesn't change clinical action. Fix = label it ("across N *separate* weeks") or reconcile the two bucketings. Touches `render.ts:537` (chronicity `flagRow`) — a B-182 render, wants its own small change + Dr. Chen wording sign-off, not a rider on the diet/weight/stool PR. | B-218 | **Vet report: the `vet_reports_public_share` RLS policy is a mass-disclosure landmine — must be fixed BEFORE PR 6's public link ships** | `001_schema.sql:239-243` grants `SELECT` on `vet_reports` `USING (share_token IS NOT NULL AND token_expires_at > NOW())` with no `TO` clause (→ `public`/`anon`). `share_token` is `NOT NULL DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4()`, so `share_token IS NOT NULL` is **always true** → a bare `GET /rest/v1/vet_reports?select=*` with only the anon key would enumerate **every user's** `pet_id`, `storage_path`, `share_token` and date ranges (a health-artifact + valid-token dump that then unlocks the Storage PDFs). **Dormant in PR 5** (PR 5 never touches `vet_reports` and mints no token), so not a PR-5 defect — but it becomes a live leak the instant PR 6 adds the unauthenticated `view-report` route. **Fix for PR 6:** DROP `vet_reports_public_share`; serve the public view through a service-role Edge Function that validates the token server-side (`.eq('share_token', token).gt('token_expires_at', now())`, single-row), enforce expiry/revocation there, and scope the token to the one minted artifact (never a live query key into the whole record). Surfaced by `rls-privacy-reviewer` on PR 5 (#265). | **Next** | 2026-07-03 | **Step 9 PR 6 (public share link) — hard blocker** | **Done — 2026-07-05 (PR #283).** Migration `026_drop_vet_reports_public_share.sql` (renumbered 025→026 to clear a same-number collision with #282's concurrently-merged `025_event_attachments_access_hardening.sql`) DROPs the leaky policy; applied live via the Supabase MCP (`vet_reports` now retains only `vet_reports_owner` → owner-only, RLS still enabled, 0 rows, `get_advisors(security)` clean — no `vet_reports` finding). The anon mass-disclosure path is closed. `rls-privacy-reviewer` run (security-sensitive access-control path). **Scope (PM, 2026-07-05):** this task fixes the leak ONLY — the service-role token-validated `view-report` read path + token minting stay PR 6; **B-143 manual revoke declined (2026-07-05)**, so the existing 30-day `token_expires_at` default is the sole expiry mechanism. | B-223 | Dual intake capture — objective intake + subjective owner-perceived-appetite rating | PM idea (2026-07-04, out of the #1 `0/25`-suppress decision): expand dietary-preference data by pairing the existing objective intake question with a *subjective* owner-perceived-appetite rating (high/med/low style — user-friendly but science-backed, ideally a validated appetite-scale instrument). | B-224 | Vet report: the "Reading the trend" (GP-0) confound note should weigh onset-aligned off-diet exposures, not only started interventions | Surfaced by `vet-report-cold-read` on the round-2 artifact (B-221). The GP-0 note is driven by `concurrentChanges` — diet-trial / medication / supplement / free-fed **interventions that started**. On the Nyx report it names the two *constant* free-fed diets (both ongoing since before onset) but omits the exposure that actually tracks symptom onset: the ~340 Temptations treats (May 15–Jun 24, starting the day after first vomiting). Two unchanged diets can't explain a *change*; the onset-aligned treat run can. It is NOT withheld (Appendix B date-span + the staple-washout line carry it), so this is a "point the confound callout at the strong confounder, not just the weak ones" improvement, not a correctness bug. Care needed: treats aren't a started-intervention, so naive inclusion would over-fire on every treat — the right trigger is an off-diet exposure run whose START aligns with (or precedes) symptom onset. Adversarial-mandatory when built (it changes what the highest-consequence note points at). | Later | 2026-07-04 | Step 9 / Step 10 confounder model | Open |

| B-228 | "Ask AI" open-ended chat assistant — competitive-parity feature | PM (2026-07-04): competitors (Lumsters, Companain) now ship an open-ended "Ask [Pet]'s AI anything" chat surface — a free-text box the owner can ask any pet-care question, distinct from Nyx's existing bounded LLM surfaces (AI Signal phrasing = one templated sentence over a pre-computed finding; `extract-food-from-photo`/`extract-medication-from-photo` = structured vision extraction). This would be Nyx's first genuinely **open-ended** conversational LLM surface — no fixed template, no `tool_choice`-forced schema, arbitrary owner questions in, arbitrary model prose out. That is a materially different risk profile from anything shipped so far and needs its own spec before a build-ready decision, not just a UI clone: (1) **n=1-never-reassures / intake-is-not-preference** — a free-text chat is far easier to accidentally reassure through than a template (`validatePhrasing` only guards the templated Signal path; an open chat has no equivalent guardrail yet); (2) **data-minimization** — does the assistant get context (this pet's logged events/photos) or answer generically? If pet-specific, what crosses the LLM boundary (raw logs/photos vs. computed findings only) — same data-minimization gate as the two open council-report Questions below; (3) **scope/wedge fit** — is this the reactive-tracking wedge or a generic pet-care chatbot feature that dilutes it (Designer/PM call); (4) **Pets > $** — if gated behind premium, the safety-relevant answers can't be (Principle 7), same constraint as the gestalt-reviewer/council-report Questions; (5) relationship to the two already-open Questions on LLM-over-findings surfaces ("AI Signals card — scope of any LLM-over-findings surface" and "Surface a council-style multi-perspective report to OWNERS?") — this may be a third rung of that same ladder (bounded finding-phrasing → gestalt reviewer → free-form Q&A) rather than a fully separate feature, and should be scoped together with them rather than designed in isolation. | B-236 | First-class, honestly-labeled "Last 90 days" report preset | The B-222 range control (PR 5d) ships **Recommended + Custom…** only. A dedicated "Last 90 days" chip was dropped because passing any explicit window makes `generate-report` label the report **"Custom range"** (any override ⇒ `resolveScope` basis `'custom'` + the §6 cherry-pick disclosure) — so a standard 90-day snapshot reads to the vet as a hand-picked crop. A first-class preset needs a small server change: `resolveScope` learns a preset marker returning its own `ScopeBasis` (e.g. `'preset_90d'`) labeled "Last 90 days" in the sublabel, the render range box, and (if kept) the disclosure header. **Recommended semantics:** the named preset does NOT fire the cherry-pick disclosure — a standard window isn't a hand-picked crop; disclosure stays reserved for a hand-drawn Custom window. Client re-adds the chip. Ride the next `generate-report` redeploy (already pending for round-2 / B-225) so it costs no extra deploy. Meanwhile the 90-day case is covered: it's what "Recommended" resolves to with no visit/trial, and "Custom…" opens pre-filled to the last 90 days. | Later | 2026-07-04 | `generate-report` redeploy (rides the round-2 / B-225 deploy) | Open |
| B-237 | Debounce Custom-range regeneration on rapid From/To changes | B-222's range control regenerates the report whenever the custom window changes. PR 5d already softens the visual churn (the report stays on screen under an "Updating…" pill instead of unmounting to a spinner — pm-feature-review's top finding, fixed), and the request memo is keyed on date STRINGS so a same-day re-fire doesn't regenerate. Residual: changing **From** then **To** in quick succession still fires two server round-trips. A short debounce (or an explicit "Update" affordance) on the custom window would coalesce them. | B-240 | Weight reads inconsistently across Profile vs Patterns (snapshot vs tracked reading) | PM QA (2026-07-04): the Patterns dashboard `WeightCard` shows the "No weigh-ins logged yet" empty state while the Profile `WeightTrendCard` shows a weight — confusing. **Root cause (by design, not a bug):** the Profile card falls back to the `pets.weight_kg` **snapshot** (set at onboarding / Edit profile, labelled "From {pet}'s profile"), but the Patterns card *deliberately* shows only real `weight_checks` rows (`WeightCard.tsx:46-58` — "a static profile number would read as a tracked reading it isn't"). | B-250 | `vet_reports` UPDATE is broken — `trg_vet_reports_updated_at` sets `NEW.updated_at` but the table has no `updated_at` column | Pre-existing schema/trigger mismatch (`001_schema.sql`: the `vet_reports` table has no `updated_at` column, yet `trg_vet_reports_updated_at` runs `set_updated_at()`, which assigns `NEW.updated_at`). | B-267 | iOS camera + photo-library permission usage strings missing from `app.json` | `expo-image-picker` drives camera (`requestCameraPermissionsAsync`/`launchCameraAsync`) and library (`requestMediaLibraryPermissionsAsync`) across food-capture, medication-capture, incident photos, and pet photos, but `app.json` sets no `NSCameraUsageDescription`/`NSPhotoLibraryUsageDescription` (only `ITSAppUsesNonExemptEncryption`) and does **not** list the `expo-image-picker` config plugin in `plugins` — so no purpose strings are injected at prebuild. iOS **crashes** an app that requests a permission with no purpose string, and App Review rejects a missing/blank one (Guideline 5.1.1). Fix: add `expo-image-picker` to `plugins` with explicit `cameraPermission`/`photosPermission`/`microphonePermission` copy (the plugin sets all three — camera capture can include video; Nyx-voice, states *why* — "so you can add a photo of a meal, symptom, or medication label"; Apple rejects generic "needs camera access" strings), verify the prebuilt Info.plist carries all keys. Verify on the actual build, don't assume EAS autolinking supplies them. **Advisory pass (2026-07-07):** the same built-artifact check should also confirm the aggregated `PrivacyInfo.xcprivacy` privacy manifest is present (Expo SDK 54 auto-aggregates required-reason declarations; verify, don't assume). | **Now** | 2026-07-07 | First App Store submission / any TestFlight build that hits camera or library | **Config fixed — shipped via #299** (rebased onto the Culprit-rebrand `main`, 2026-07-08): the `expo-image-picker` config plugin now injects `NSCameraUsageDescription` + `NSPhotoLibraryUsageDescription` with **Culprit**-branded, purpose-stating copy; `microphonePermission=false` suppresses the unused mic string (re-verified on current `main` that every image-picker call site is `mediaTypes: ['images']` — no video capture, so the mic string would be unused). `expo config --type introspect` confirms both keys inject (resolved app name `Culprit`) and the mic key does not. **Scope-limited to the permission strings — does NOT include B-269's `supportsTablet: false` flip** (still its own change). **Residuals (PM/on-build, introspect can't check either):** (1) verify both keys on the actual prebuilt/EAS `Info.plist`; (2) confirm the aggregated `PrivacyInfo.xcprivacy` privacy manifest is present (Expo SDK 54 auto-aggregates — verify, don't assume). |

| B-271 | App Review demo account + reviewer notes | Nyx is login-gated: Apple requires working sign-in credentials in App Review Information (Guideline 2.1), and a reviewer landing in an **empty** account sees only empty states and can't evaluate the Signal / trends / vet report ("we were unable to evaluate the app's features" is a common rejection). Pre-seed a demo account with a demo pet + ~2–4 weeks of realistic logs (meals, a few symptoms, a weight) so the intelligence surfaces actually render, and write reviewer notes (what the app does, where the AI reads appear, the credentials). | B-341 | Context-adaptive intake timing — resolve a grazed meal's intake at the *next* feeding, not at log time | The WSAVA intake chips fire co-located with the meal log (`MealCompletionCard`), which is the right moment for **scarfers** (dog kibble, cat treats — consumption ≈ instantaneous) but **premature for grazers** (cat wet food): the owner doesn't know how much was eaten until the next feeding, when they see the leftover bowl. A single co-located capture point is structurally biased against cats (Dr. Chen's "single `offered_at`" bias, `2026-05-feeding-windows` §6) → the highest-value `feline_reduced_intake` flag (B-027/B-033) stays silent for exactly the pet most at risk, because the owner skips/guesses/forgets the premature ask. Proposed: a **"eaten over time / grazed" property on the (pet, food) pair** (food-domain toggle, sibling to free-choice B-040; sensible default inferred from species + `food_type`), a **pending-intake state that never assumes finished** (B-156 G1 fail-safe generalized), and **resolution at the next-meal ritual** ("answering beats initiating", `logging-capture-discovery` §2 — zero new nag). Honest modelling: consumed-at is a *window* (offered→assessed), not a point → ties to B-010 `occurred_at_confidence` + the free-feeding "intake not directly observed" caveat for acute correlation. **This is the wet-food offered-vs-consumed timing window the free-feeding R1 explicitly fenced off** (`nyx-free-feeding-requirements.md` §0) — Eng blast-radius flag: touches the meal/event model, not a pure additive edge. Safety: a grazer leaving wet food is the canonical false-reassurance trap — resolution copy routes refused/picked toward a health flag, never softens to "picky" (intake-is-not-preference). | Next | 2026-07-13 | Composes with B-014 / B-015 / B-033 / B-040; ties to the 2026-07-10 "are owner-configured confirmations nudges?" Open Question | Open — surfaced 2026-07-13 (PM dogfooding: Nyx grazes wet food, assessed at the next feeding). Persona + product-team discussion held this session. **PM direction 2026-07-13:** (1) **in-app resolve-at-next-log endorsed as the core**; PM also wants to explore **multi-channel** (in-app **+** a notification, possibly staggered timing) for a higher resolution/conversion rate than any single channel — endorsed *with two non-negotiables baked in*: **cross-channel de-dup** (a resolution in one channel silences the other — never nag about an already-answered bowl) and **fail-safe silence** (an ignored notification records *nothing*, never "finished" — B-156 G1). The *notification* channel inherits the deferred **2026-07-10 Open Question** (are owner-configured confirmations "nudges" under Principle 4's cap?); the in-app ride does not. (2) **Property carrier** (how the app knows a food is "eaten over time") left as a **build-time decision**, not blocking — team lean: **infer a smart default** from species + `food_type`, **one-time owner-correctable toggle** in the food domain (sibling to free-choice), avoid a per-instance "check back later" (re-adds a moment-of-event decision). (3) WSAVA explainer split to **B-342**; "go deeper later." Discovery doc (`nyx-intake-timing-requirements.md`) deferred until the roadmap slot — PM: go deeper later, if needed. |
| B-342 | Explain the WSAVA 5-point intake scale in-app | Owners don't know the `refused / picked / some / most / all` boundaries; the clinically load-bearing **refused-vs-picked line** (didn't-eat vs ate-a-little — the escalation-adjacent boundary) gets blurred, mis-calibrating the ratings that feed `feline_reduced_intake` (B-027). Cheap fix (tap-to-reveal info affordance + sharper per-chip microcopy), real clinical payoff (better-calibrated input to the highest-value flag). Designer constraint: **must not clutter the 10-second path** — explanation is pull-to-reveal, never always-on text. nyx-voice + Dr. Chen sign-off on the boundary definitions (esp. refused vs picked). | Next | 2026-07-13 | Pairs with B-341; touches `IntakeChipRow` / `MealCompletionCard` | Open — surfaced 2026-07-13 (PM side-idea). |
| B-279 | Harden the chunked SecureStore auth adapter — concurrency + orphan bound | Two non-blocking residuals from the #306 `code-reviewer` re-review of `lib/secureStore.ts` (the frequent-signin fix). **(1) No concurrency mutex:** two overlapping `setItem` calls on the same key (e.g. an auto-refresh write racing a user sign-in) could both compute `prev.gen + 1` and collide on one generation's key set, reintroducing a mixing risk *between two live writers* (distinct from the write+crash case, which IS fixed). Safe in practice only because supabase-js typically serializes its own storage calls during refresh — an external assumption this module doesn't defend. Add an in-module per-key write queue if session-persistence bugs ever resurface under rapid sign-in/out/refresh interleaving. **(2) Unbounded generation counter:** `gen` increments forever and cleanup is best-effort, so a *sustained* run of cleanup failures would accumulate orphaned chunk keys indefinitely (never read — the pointer names only the live gen — so correctness-safe, storage-only). Low real-world likelihood; only worth a pass if the file is reopened. | Later | 2026-07-08 | — (only if session-persistence bugs resurface under concurrent auth ops) | Open — **the "if session-persistence bugs resurface" trigger HAS fired**: frequent logouts confirmed still-present on **build 32** (#306 did NOT fix them; #327 shipped on-device instrumentation to find the real cause — server logs show cold-start session-restore failure on iOS). The concurrency-mutex residual (#1) is a leading fix candidate, but this whole row may be **superseded** if the #327 trail points to reverting the chunked adapter to a verified single-key one. Originally surfaced by the #306 code-reviewer re-review (2026-07-08); both residuals non-blocking + correctness-safe. **Update 2026-07-15: the resurfaced logout was DIAGNOSED (build-33 trail) as keychain accessibility — `WHEN_UNLOCKED` blocked the locked-device background refresh — NOT the concurrency residual, and FIXED in #350 (`AFTER_FIRST_UNLOCK`). The chunked adapter is RETAINED, not reverted (the "revert to single-key" speculation above is moot — chunking was confirmed working in the same trail). The two original residuals (#1 concurrency mutex, #2 orphan bound) remain Open + non-blocking; revisit only if logouts persist after build 34.** |

| B-254 | Bind `vet_reports` INSERT `pet_id` + `storage_path` to the owner (defense-in-depth for the public link) | `rls-privacy-reviewer` on PR 6: `vet_reports_owner` (`FOR ALL USING (auth.uid() = generated_by)`) gates only `generated_by` on INSERT — a user can `POST /rest/v1/vet_reports` directly with `generated_by = self`, an arbitrary `pet_id`, and an **attacker-chosen `storage_path`**, then read back their own row's default `share_token` and drive `view-report` to `download()` that key from `nyx-vet-reports`. **Not exploitable today**: the bucket is hardcoded (no cross-bucket traversal), keys are two server-generated UUIDv4s (~244 bits — a victim's report key is unguessable), and `view-report` only ever downloads a *named* key (never lists). So it's "safe by entropy," not "safe by construction." Fix (own schema/RLS PR + `rls-privacy-reviewer`, mirroring B-244): a `WITH CHECK` / `BEFORE INSERT` binding `pet_id IN (SELECT id FROM pets WHERE user_id = auth.uid())` **and** `storage_path LIKE pet_id || '/%'`. Turns the crafted-path insert impossible by construction. Same class as the PR-7 `event_attachments` prefix-binding note (`generate-report/index.ts` header). | Next | 2026-07-05 | Step 9 (before scale / the public link is exercised broadly) | Open — surfaced by `rls-privacy-reviewer` on PR 6; non-blocking (244-bit key entropy), defense-in-depth. |
| B-255 | Reap expired / superseded `vet_reports` rows + their `nyx-vet-reports` artifacts | Two retention gaps surfaced by PR 6 reviews. (1) An **expired** report row + its stored HTML linger after `token_expires_at` — `view-report` returns 410 and the bucket is private, so it is *unreachable*, but the pet-health artifact is still retained (data-minimization / B-039 territory, like B-249's orphaned event photos). (2) Minting is INSERT-only with **no manual revoke** (B-143 declined), so every tap of "share a link" mints a *new* row + artifact, all live for the full 30 days — repeated taps/cancels quietly accumulate live public health-data URLs. A periodic sweep (or a mint-time "supersede the pet's prior unexpired link") would purge rows/objects past expiry and cap accumulation. Not a leak; retention hygiene. | Later | 2026-07-05 | T&S / B-039 deletion & retention | Open — surfaced by `rls-privacy-reviewer` + `code-reviewer` on PR 6. |

| B-253 | Public vet-report share link — deferred (Supabase serves HTML as text/plain); rebuild PDF-based | **PM decision 2026-07-06: defer the public browser link.** The v1 sharing mechanism is the working **"Send to vet" → on-device PDF → native share sheet** (PR 5/7); the public link was always secondary (spec §8.2). **Why deferred — a hard platform constraint found in live testing (not a code bug):** Supabase serves `text/html` as **`text/plain`** from BOTH Edge Functions (docs: "GET requests that return text/html will be rewritten to text/plain") AND Storage (docs: "HTML files are returned as plain text") as an anti-XSS/phishing measure — so a browser-viewable **HTML** report link served from Supabase is impossible as spec §7 assumed ("stream the artifact / short-lived signed URL"). **Future rebuild = PDF-based** (browsers render PDFs inline from a signed Storage URL; only HTML is special-cased): mint = the client's on-device `expo-print` PDF (the SAME trusted artifact as the share sheet) uploaded to `nyx-vet-reports` + a `vet_reports` token row; `view-report` = validate token + 30-day expiry → **302 → short-lived (~60s) signed PDF URL** (§8-compliant, never a baked long-TTL URL). The security design from the reverted build holds (both gates passed: `rls-privacy-reviewer` = PASS, `code-reviewer` folded) — reuse its token-validation/expiry logic + the B-218 posture; the reverted HTML mint/`view-report` source lives in PR #285's history. **Composes with B-254** (bind `vet_reports` INSERT `pet_id`/`storage_path`) + **B-255** (reap expired artifacts) when built. **Deployed-but-inert cleanup:** the `view-report` v1 (verify_jwt=false) function was deployed during investigation and is now a no-op (nothing mints → always 404; harmless — B-218 closed anon enumeration) — delete it via the dashboard at leisure, or leave it. | Later | 2026-07-06 | Step 9 public link (revisit post-MVP / when prioritized) | Open — deferred by PM 2026-07-06; the platform constraint is recorded here so it is never re-litigated. B-250 (its schema dep) shipped + applied to prod. |

| B-311 | Tokenise `colorEventMedication` (first med-coloured surface) | The Calendar v3 drill-in (N5b) is the first surface to colour a *medication* event, and the mock invented an untokenised medication indigo chip (`#EEF0FF`/`#5B63C4`) — `constants/theme.ts` has only symptom-rose and meal-teal, no medication token. Indigo is also "world/ground only" per §1.3 (teal is the sole interactive accent on light records surfaces), so a med chip shouldn't be indigo-family and a *selected day* (interactive state) must read teal (`colorAccentSoft`), not the mock's lavender `#ECEBFA`. | B-337 | Vet-report share: auto-generated cover-note / talking points | PM n=1 from the first real report send (2026-07-13): generating + PDF-sharing the report is frictionless, but the owner is dropped into a blank email and spends too long drafting the cover note — they wished for ready talking points. | B-338 | analyze-vomit: separate scene objects from vomit contents (a false-positive CLASS, not a detune) | PM n=1 (2026-07-13): two AI foreign-material reads were both wrong — a blue ball that was a **toy elsewhere in the frame** (not in the vomit at all) and a "stick" that was the **seasoning layer of turkey deli meat**. The first is a genuine prompt/segmentation bug (a scene object read as content); the second is a fine-grained vision limit. **Direction constraint (non-negotiable):** we deliberately escalate-on-presence — false positives are the SAFE error — and B-042 pushes for *more* sensitivity, so this is NOT a licence to detune. Scope narrowly to the safe fix only: prompt the model to distinguish "material that is IN the vomit" from "objects elsewhere in the photo," and/or a confirm-screen affordance to mark scene-only objects; leave sensitivity to material actually in the vomit untouched. `adversarial-reviewer` + `clinical-guardrails` mandatory — must not open an under-escalation path (a real foreign body is an emergency). | Next | 2026-07-13 | — | Open — surfaced 2026-07-13 (PM n=1); pairs with B-042 (opposite direction — read together). |
| B-339 | Stale `visual_flags`/`recommendation` cache after an owner edit (override propagation) | PM n=1 (2026-07-13): overrode the false foreign-material flag (B-028 editable fields). **Verified this session:** the client edit (`buildVomitEditWrite`, `lib/analysis.ts:152`) writes ONLY the owner-editable structured fields + `edited_at` — it deliberately does NOT recompute the cached `visual_flags` / `recommendation` / `read_text`. Consequence split: **(a) the vet report is ALREADY override-aware** — `generate-report` derives a photo's safety class from the structured fields (`foreign_material_present`/`blood_present`/`edited_at`) and never `SELECT`s `visual_flags` (`index.ts:724`), so a cleared flag drops the photo from the safety lead by construction (a sent PDF is a snapshot, so only edits BEFORE generation reach it — not a bug). **(b) the row's cached `visual_flags`/`recommendation` stay STALE** — still `suspected_foreign_material` / `worth_a_call` after the owner clears the fact. Anything keying off those is NOT override-aware: today the event DETAIL screen recommendation badge (minor, escalate-safe / firm), and — critically — the future Signal elevation (B-340). Fix options: recompute `visual_flags`/`recommendation` from the edited structured fields on the edit write (fights the never-clobber stance), OR make consumers derive from structured fields (the report's model — preferred). **B-340 adopts derive-from-structured-fields, so it needs no cache fix; this row is the residual detail-screen staleness + a general "the cache lies after an edit" cleanup.** | Next | 2026-07-13 | Detail-screen recommendation staleness; consistency with B-340 | Open — verified 2026-07-13; report is fine, cache is stale. |
| B-340 | Elevate per-incident vomit red flags into the Home Signal safety surface | **PM-RATIFIED 2026-07-13** (Open Q resolved — elevate). Today `generate-signal/detection.ts` never reads `event_ai_analysis`, so a per-incident blood / suspected-foreign-material flag lives only on the event detail screen and never reaches Home (Principle 3 — "safety insights always lead"). Build a new safety-class detector that reads the pet's in-window non-deleted vomit incidents' AI analysis and fires a firm-but-calm Home safety card when a VISUAL red flag is present, led at top. **Non-negotiable build guardrails:** (1) derive the flag from the owner-editable structured fields (`foreign_material_present==='yes'`; `blood_present∈{fresh_red,coffee_ground}`), NOT the stale `visual_flags` array — so an owner override clears the card by construction (mirrors `generate-report`; see B-339); (2) escalate-on-presence, never reassure (a cleared/absent flag is silence, never an all-clear — `clinical-guardrails`); (3) tone = existing firm safety register, no new "danger" state; (4) single-incident fires (no corroboration gate — false positives are cheap for the owner to clear). **Scope (Engineer rec):** visual flags only (the net-new datum); the contextual `worth_a_call` escalations (repeated-vomiting / feline-reduced-intake / lethargy) are a separate lane question, not this item. **Reads a NEW source into `detectSignals` → `adversarial-reviewer` MANDATORY.** **Deploy-gated:** the client (`lib/signal.ts` InsightType + `InsightCard` renderer) must render the new type BEFORE `generate-signal` is redeployed (the B-182 "registered but unrenderable" lesson). | B-343 | `food_items` global-catalog write is not ownership-checked (any authed user can overwrite any row) | Surfaced by the `rls-privacy-reviewer` during T2-3 (2026-07-14) as a **pre-existing, non-T2-3** finding. `extract-food-from-photo` (and the client commit path) can drive a service-role UPDATE of ANY global `food_items` row given only a body `food_item_id` — the table is globally scoped by design (no `pet_id`/`user_id`; the sanctioned shared-catalog exception), so there is no ownership predicate on the row. T2-3's `validateFoodPhotoPaths` binds the photo *paths* to the claimed `food_item_id` but does NOT (and structurally cannot) prove the caller owns/created that row. Impact today: catalog-integrity only (a malicious/ buggy client could clobber a shared food's extracted fields), not a PII/access leak — the bucket is globally-authenticated-readable and the row carries no owner data. Fix direction (defer): gate catalog writes on `created_by_user_id = auth.uid()` for `ai_extracted`/user-created rows, or route mutations through an owner-checked RPC; interacts with the food dedup/merge spec (B-009/B-018) which already contemplates multi-user survivorship. **Composes with B-351** (owner-editable `primary_protein` is another manual write to the same unguarded global row). | Later | 2026-07-14 | Composes with B-009/B-018 (dedup/merge multi-user auth), B-351 | Open — surfaced 2026-07-14 (rls-privacy-reviewer, T2-3). **2026-07-16: closure path set by B-354** (`docs/nyx-per-account-food-library-requirements.md` FR-2 client half + FR-6 server half — the ownership predicate this row lacked now exists by design); close when B-354 PRs 1+3 ship. |

| B-345 | Strict ship-dark for the paywall gate during the first-run config-load race (T2-5) | `useAppConfig` resolves `paywall_enabled` asynchronously (auth-driven fetch + cached last-known-good). Because the paywall flag alone fails **closed** (unlike the fail-open AI flags), a brand-new signup with no cache that reaches `app/onboarding/pet-age.tsx` before the config fetch lands reads the `false` default and routes past the seeded-`true` mocked paywall. Per the T2-5 AC this is the "config-unreachable → hidden" clause (not a byte-identical break of the steady state — returning users hydrate from cache instantly, and the single SELECT beats five screens of typing on any real network), and the failure is soft (a mock CTA shown less often, never a dead/broken screen) and degrades toward the eventual submission goal — so it was **accepted as a residual**, not fixed. If the PM later wants strict byte-identical even for that first-run-in-flight window, the fix is to expose a `configReady`/hydrated boolean from `useAppConfig` and have onboarding treat "not yet resolved" explicitly — but note a naive "default to on while loading" would re-open the fail-closed rejection-risk in the other direction, so any fix must default to **hidden-until-resolved** and only *delay* the paywall decision, not force it on. Low stakes: this is a mock with no purchase path until T3-D un-mocks it. | Later | 2026-07-15 | T3-D paywall un-mock (matters more once the paywall is real) | Open — surfaced 2026-07-15 (code-reviewer, T2-5; accepted soft residual). |
| B-352 | Pass source width/height to `compressForUpload` at the non-dimensioned upload sites | `code-reviewer` (privacy-hardening sweep, 2026-07-15). `compressForUpload(uri)` at `app/vet-visit.tsx`, `app/edit-event.tsx`, `app/log.tsx`, and `app/event/[id].tsx` is called WITHOUT `sourceWidth`/`sourceHeight`, so its `isPortrait` branch never triggers and it always resizes on `width` — a portrait photo can end up taller than 1600px on the long edge (a storage-efficiency nit; for a vet DOCUMENT it errs toward *more* legible, so no correctness/privacy risk). Pre-existing pattern, NOT introduced by the privacy PR (food-capture / medication-capture / food[id] / medication[id] already pass dims from the picker asset). Fix: thread the picker asset's `width`/`height` through to `compressForUpload` at these four sites for a correctly-bounded long edge. | Later | 2026-07-15 | — | Open — surfaced 2026-07-15 (code-reviewer, privacy-hardening sweep). |
| B-351 | Structured multi-protein capture + set-membership correlation (beyond `primary_protein`) | Surfaced by the PM during B-332 (2026-07-15). Today the food model carries a SINGLE `primary_protein` (extraction-only until B-332; owner-editable after), and the flagship diet correlation keys off that one field. **Dr. Chen:** for the elimination / novel-protein trial — our wedge — hidden *secondary* proteins are the single most common reason a home trial silently fails (a "duck" food that also lists chicken by-product meal contaminates the trial), so "primary only" systematically misses the exposure that matters most; the advisors would favour capturing ALL proteins. **Data Scientist (counterweight):** not a free win — a multi-protein exposure model is harder to attribute (co-occurring proteins are collinear, foods with 4–5 proteins bloat the exposure set, per-protein effective-n drops); it raises *sensitivity to hidden exposure* but muddies *which* protein is the culprit. Done properly this is ONE cross-cutting change — extraction emits all proteins → schema holds them (`proteins` jsonb/array or a join table; NOT `primary_protein` alone) → the correlation engine (`lib/analytics.ts`, `generate-signal/detection.ts`) keys on set-membership → the vet report renders them — and likely absorbs **B-048** (ingredient→protein canonicalization). Note the full ingredient list is ALREADY captured as free text (`food_items.ingredients_notes`), just not structured, so no raw data is being lost today. Deliberately NOT folded into B-332 (which is single-protein parity-with-extraction to unblock the T3-E gate). Gated on the CLAUDE.md Open Question (vet-advisor + PM: sensitivity vs. attribution). `adversarial-reviewer` mandatory (statistical) + Dr. Chen. | Later | 2026-07-15 | Vet-report protein exposure; Step 10 correlation quality; likely absorbs B-048 | Open — surfaced 2026-07-15 (PM during B-332); needs the Open-Question decision before it's spec-ready. |

| B-354 | Per-account food library (de-globalize the `food_items` catalog before launch) | `food_items` (and its `medication_items` twin) is a **globally-scoped** catalog — a CLAUDE.md "sanctioned exception" (a shared food catalog). PM confirmed the consequence 2026-07-16: sign in with a *different* account and you see every other account's foods in your picker (`refreshFoodCache` selects all `food_items` with no user filter; sign-out wipes the cache so each account re-hydrates the same global set). **Trust & Safety frames this as a pre-launch blocker, not just UX:** a global catalog exposes each user's added foods (their pet's actual diet — health-adjacent) plus `created_by_user_id` cross-tenant, which a privacy / App-Store review would flag; Designer/Jordan/Sam add that a stranger's foods (and typos) in your picker fail the 10-second test; Data Scientist notes per-account isolation also removes cross-user metadata contamination of correlations and makes dedup within-account (cleaner n). Team lean (near-unanimous, PM-validated) = **per-account library now; the shared / network-effect catalog is a possible future / premium iteration.** Scope: additive owner-scope on `food_items` (promote `created_by_user_id` or add `owner_user_id`) + RLS `USING owner = auth.uid()` (currently world-readable to any authed user) + `refreshFoodCache` filters by user + backfill existing rows to their creator (null-creator/seeded rows need a home) + reconcile with the deferred household primitive (B-292: scope unit = account now, revisit per-household later) + the identical `medication_items` twin (cover here or spawn a sibling). Ripple: reshapes the dedup track (B-009/B-018 assume a global catalog + cross-user dedup) and makes **B-005's per-user archive fall out for free** (a per-account `archived_at` IS per-user — so B-354 should precede or bundle B-005 to avoid building a throwaway per-user-archive join table). Changes a CLAUDE.md hard constraint → Tier-1 edit on ratification. `rls-privacy-reviewer` mandatory on the re-scoping migration. | Now | 2026-07-16 | First App Store submission; B-005 per-user archive; dedup track (B-009/B-018) | Open — **requirements delivered 2026-07-16** (`docs/nyx-per-account-food-library-requirements.md`; PM requirements session): direction **PM-ratified** (per-account now; future shared catalog = a separate curated layer, never un-scoping user rows), 9 FRs + 5-PR plan (schema/RLS/storage → client cache filter + one-time flush → extract-food ownership gate → delete-account purge flip → docs/legal). Live-data grounding: 56 rows / 1 creator / 0 null-creator / **0 cross-account meal/trial/arrangement refs** (of 624) → backfill is trivial; cheapest now. Closes B-343 by construction (FR-2+FR-6); B-005 archive falls out per-user for free (spec §6). **D2/D4/D6 PM-ratified same day (2026-07-16):** meds bundle into PR 1; deletion flips preserve→purge + the small legal rewrite (hosted republish = PM action at PR 5); B-354 → B-005 back to back. **PR 1 (schema migration) ready to build.** |
